\doxysubsection{Detailed Description}
\subsubsection*{template$<$typename Derived$>$\newline
class Eigen\+::\+Matrix\+Base$<$ Derived $>$}
Base class for all dense matrices, vectors, and expressions. 

This class is the base that is inherited by all matrix, vector, and related expression types. Most of the \doxylink{namespaceEigen}{Eigen} API is contained in this class, and its base classes. Other important classes for the \doxylink{namespaceEigen}{Eigen} API are \doxylink{classEigen_1_1Matrix}{Matrix}, and \doxylink{classEigen_1_1VectorwiseOp}{Vectorwise\+Op}.

Note that some methods are defined in other modules such as the LU\+\_\+\+Module LU module for all functions related to matrix inversions.


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em Derived} & is the derived type, e.\+g. a matrix type, or an expression, etc.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}
When writing a function taking \doxylink{namespaceEigen}{Eigen} objects as argument, if you want your function to take as argument any matrix, vector, or expression, just let it take a \doxylink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Matrix\+Base} argument. As an example, here is a function print\+First\+Row which, given a matrix, vector, or expression {\itshape x}, prints the first row of {\itshape x}.


\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{keyword}{template}<\textcolor{keyword}{typename}\ Derived>}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{keywordtype}{void}\ printFirstRow(\textcolor{keyword}{const}\ \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Eigen::MatrixBase<Derived>}}\&\ x)}
\DoxyCodeLine{\{}
\DoxyCodeLine{\ \ cout\ <<\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceEigen_1_1numext_ac5e96d65e0b577673dd47bfe1068cdd9}{x}}.row(0)\ <<\ endl;}
\DoxyCodeLine{\}}

\end{DoxyCode}


This class can be extended with the help of the plugin mechanism described on the page Topic\+Customizing\+\_\+\+Plugins by defining the preprocessor symbol {\ttfamily EIGEN\+\_\+\+MATRIXBASE\+\_\+\+PLUGIN}.

\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\Hypertarget{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a73d8782980bd75141785340d3a7a8e10}\index{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$}!adjoint@{adjoint}}
\index{adjoint@{adjoint}!Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{adjoint()}{adjoint()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a73d8782980bd75141785340d3a7a8e10} 
template$<$typename Derived $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a9efec3cfd22b9a33bead9c6718d128da}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC}} const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Matrix\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_ad40569982585e9820f7ea86176ca64fc}{\+::\+Adjoint\+Return\+Type}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Eigen\+::\+Matrix\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::adjoint (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
an expression of the adjoint (i.\+e. conjugate transpose) of \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this.
\end{DoxyReturn}
Example\+: 
\begin{DoxyCodeInclude}{0}

\end{DoxyCodeInclude}
 Output\+: 
\begin{DoxyVerbInclude}
\end{DoxyVerbInclude}


\begin{DoxyWarning}{Warning}
If you want to replace a matrix by its own adjoint, do {\bfseries{NOT}} do this\+: 
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{m\ =\ m.adjoint();\ \textcolor{comment}{//\ bug!!!\ caused\ by\ aliasing\ effect}}

\end{DoxyCode}
 Instead, use the \doxylink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_ad2a2f67a3a6e5f65f41ab47e78bbf904}{adjoint\+In\+Place()} method\+: 
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{m.adjointInPlace();}

\end{DoxyCode}
 which gives \doxylink{namespaceEigen}{Eigen} good opportunities for optimization, or alternatively you can also do\+: 
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{m\ =\ m.adjoint().eval();}

\end{DoxyCode}

\end{DoxyWarning}

\Hypertarget{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a984cf8ba296d2a7ec86aa5eda8ce3fd8}\index{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$}!adjoint@{adjoint}}
\index{adjoint@{adjoint}!Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{adjoint()}{adjoint()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [2/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a984cf8ba296d2a7ec86aa5eda8ce3fd8} 
template$<$typename Derived $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a9efec3cfd22b9a33bead9c6718d128da}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC}} const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_ad40569982585e9820f7ea86176ca64fc}{Adjoint\+Return\+Type}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Eigen\+::\+Matrix\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::adjoint (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const}

\Hypertarget{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_ad2a2f67a3a6e5f65f41ab47e78bbf904}\index{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$}!adjointInPlace@{adjointInPlace}}
\index{adjointInPlace@{adjointInPlace}!Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{adjointInPlace()}{adjointInPlace()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_ad2a2f67a3a6e5f65f41ab47e78bbf904} 
template$<$typename Derived $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a9efec3cfd22b9a33bead9c6718d128da}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC}} void \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Eigen\+::\+Matrix\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::adjoint\+In\+Place (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

This is the "{}in place"{} version of \doxylink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a73d8782980bd75141785340d3a7a8e10}{adjoint()}\+: it replaces {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this} by its own transpose. Thus, doing 
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{m.adjointInPlace();}

\end{DoxyCode}
 has the same effect on m as doing 
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{m\ =\ m.adjoint().eval();}

\end{DoxyCode}
 and is faster and also safer because in the latter line of code, forgetting the \doxylink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a5df64c66228ba75bbc66db2584185527}{eval()} results in a bug caused by aliasing.

Notice however that this method is only useful if you want to replace a matrix by its own adjoint. If you just need the adjoint of a matrix, use \doxylink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a73d8782980bd75141785340d3a7a8e10}{adjoint()}.

\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
if the matrix is not square, then {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this} must be a resizable matrix. This excludes (non-\/square) fixed-\/size matrices, block-\/expressions and maps.
\end{DoxyNote}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\doxylink{classEigen_1_1DenseBase_af891b9782f712151a471b3d7cfaaa2e8}{transpose()}, \doxylink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a73d8782980bd75141785340d3a7a8e10}{adjoint()}, \doxylink{classEigen_1_1DenseBase_a2bf1856f4ff79f0db0e6d416a2edfb0f}{transpose\+In\+Place()} 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\index{adjointInPlace@{adjointInPlace}!Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{adjointInPlace()}{adjointInPlace()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [2/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_ad2a2f67a3a6e5f65f41ab47e78bbf904} 
template$<$typename Derived $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a9efec3cfd22b9a33bead9c6718d128da}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC}} void \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Eigen\+::\+Matrix\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::adjoint\+In\+Place (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\Hypertarget{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a9d156c1e239110e7af8d120a51470e03}\index{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$}!applyHouseholderOnTheLeft@{applyHouseholderOnTheLeft}}
\index{applyHouseholderOnTheLeft@{applyHouseholderOnTheLeft}!Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{applyHouseholderOnTheLeft()}{applyHouseholderOnTheLeft()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a9d156c1e239110e7af8d120a51470e03} 
template$<$typename Derived $>$ \\
template$<$typename Essential\+Part $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a9efec3cfd22b9a33bead9c6718d128da}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC}} void \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Eigen\+::\+Matrix\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::apply\+Householder\+On\+The\+Left (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const Essential\+Part \&}]{essential}{, }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_ac6c9fcfb905b0e2b83652e950a52246f}{Scalar}} \&}]{tau}{, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_ac6c9fcfb905b0e2b83652e950a52246f}{Scalar}} \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{workspace}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Apply the elementary reflector H given by $ H = I - tau v v^*$ with $ v^T = [1 essential^T] $ from the left to a vector or matrix.

On input\+: 
\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em essential} & the essential part of the vector {\ttfamily v} \\
\hline
{\em tau} & the scaling factor of the Householder transformation \\
\hline
{\em workspace} & a pointer to working space with at least this-\/\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}cols() entries\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_adab847f7a3a4329e2caa3f49763ac993} 
template$<$typename Derived $>$ \\
template$<$typename Essential\+Part $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a9efec3cfd22b9a33bead9c6718d128da}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC}} void \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Eigen\+::\+Matrix\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::apply\+Householder\+On\+The\+Right (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const Essential\+Part \&}]{essential}{, }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_ac6c9fcfb905b0e2b83652e950a52246f}{Scalar}} \&}]{tau}{, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_ac6c9fcfb905b0e2b83652e950a52246f}{Scalar}} \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{workspace}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Apply the elementary reflector H given by $ H = I - tau v v^*$ with $ v^T = [1 essential^T] $ from the right to a vector or matrix.

On input\+: 
\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em essential} & the essential part of the vector {\ttfamily v} \\
\hline
{\em tau} & the scaling factor of the Householder transformation \\
\hline
{\em workspace} & a pointer to working space with at least this-\/\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}rows() entries\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a9efec3cfd22b9a33bead9c6718d128da}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC}} void \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Eigen\+::\+Matrix\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::apply\+On\+The\+Left (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceEigen_a62e77e0933482dafde8fe197d9a2cfde}{Index}}}]{p}{, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceEigen_a62e77e0933482dafde8fe197d9a2cfde}{Index}}}]{q}{, }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1JacobiRotation}{Jacobi\+Rotation}}$<$ Other\+Scalar $>$ \&}]{j}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

\textbackslash{}jacobi\+\_\+module Applies the rotation in the plane {\itshape j} to the rows {\itshape p} and {\itshape q} of {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this}, i.\+e., it computes B = J \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} B, with $ B = \left ( \begin{array}{cc} \text{*this.row}(p) \\ \text{*this.row}(q) \end{array} \right ) $.

Applies the rotation in the plane {\itshape j} to the columns {\itshape p} and {\itshape q} of {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this}, i.\+e., it computes B = B \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} J with $ B = \left ( \begin{array}{cc} \text{*this.col}(p) & \text{*this.col}(q) \end{array} \right ) $.

\Hypertarget{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a4a3ac99e4cd767a110c84421dda22ab1}\index{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$}!blueNorm@{blueNorm}}
\index{blueNorm@{blueNorm}!Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{blueNorm()}{blueNorm()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a4a3ac99e4cd767a110c84421dda22ab1} 
template$<$typename Derived $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{structEigen_1_1NumTraits}{Num\+Traits}}$<$ typenameinternal\+::traits$<$ Derived $>$\mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_ac6c9fcfb905b0e2b83652e950a52246f}{\+::\+Scalar}} $>$\+::\+Real \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Eigen\+::\+Matrix\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::blue\+Norm (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
the {\itshape l2} norm of {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this} using the Blue\textquotesingle{}s algorithm. A Portable Fortran Program to Find the Euclidean Norm of a Vector, ACM TOMS, Vol 4, Issue 1, 1978.
\end{DoxyReturn}
For architecture/scalar types without vectorization, this version is much faster than \doxylink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a624431d9543dacf9aef2bee325a0686f}{stable\+Norm()}. Otherwise the \doxylink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a624431d9543dacf9aef2bee325a0686f}{stable\+Norm()} is faster.

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}

\end{DoxySeeAlso}

template$<$typename Result\+Type $>$ \\
void \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Eigen\+::\+Matrix\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::compute\+Inverse\+And\+Det\+With\+Check (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{Result\+Type \&}]{inverse}{, }\item[{typename Result\+Type\+::\+Scalar \&}]{determinant}{, }\item[{bool \&}]{invertible}{, }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a04816f5030c114f446ab76a6cdf0f216}{Real\+Scalar}} \&}]{abs\+Determinant\+Threshold}{ = {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{structEigen_1_1NumTraits}{Num\+Traits}}$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_ac6c9fcfb905b0e2b83652e950a52246f}{Scalar}}$>$\+:\+:dummy\+\_\+precision()}}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

\textbackslash{}lu\+\_\+module

Computation of matrix inverse and determinant, with invertibility check.

This is only for fixed-\/size square matrices of size up to 4x4.

Notice that it will trigger a copy of input matrix when trying to do the inverse in place.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em inverse} & Reference to the matrix in which to store the inverse. \\
\hline
{\em determinant} & Reference to the variable in which to store the determinant. \\
\hline
{\em invertible} & Reference to the bool variable in which to store whether the matrix is invertible. \\
\hline
{\em abs\+Determinant\+Threshold} & Optional parameter controlling the invertibility check. The matrix will be declared invertible if the absolute value of its determinant is greater than this threshold.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
Example\+: 
\begin{DoxyCodeInclude}{0}

\end{DoxyCodeInclude}
 Output\+: 
\begin{DoxyVerbInclude}
\end{DoxyVerbInclude}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
an expression of the coefficient-\/wise == operator of \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this and {\itshape other} 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxyWarning}{Warning}
this performs an exact comparison, which is generally a bad idea with floating-\/point types. In order to check for equality between two vectors or matrices with floating-\/point coefficients, it is generally a far better idea to use a fuzzy comparison as provided by \doxylink{classEigen_1_1DenseBase_af3793521d788a946cb9c5f4f92bab4d3}{is\+Approx()} and \doxylink{classEigen_1_1DenseBase_acc982903f94ed372fafa901e6822ae8d}{is\+Much\+Smaller\+Than()}.
\end{DoxyWarning}

template$<$typename Derived $>$ \\
template$<$typename Other\+Derived $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a9efec3cfd22b9a33bead9c6718d128da}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC}} const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1CwiseBinaryOp}{Cwise\+Binary\+Op}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structEigen_1_1numext_1_1not__equal__to}{numext\+::not\+\_\+equal\+\_\+to}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_ac6c9fcfb905b0e2b83652e950a52246f}{Scalar}} $>$, const Derived, const Other\+Derived $>$ \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Eigen\+::\+Matrix\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::cwise\+Not\+Equal (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2ArrayBase_8h_a140b988ffa480af0799d873ce22898f2}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+CURRENT\+\_\+\+STORAGE\+\_\+\+BASE\+\_\+\+CLASS}}$<$ Other\+Derived $>$ \&}]{other}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
an expression of the coefficient-\/wise != operator of \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this and {\itshape other} 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxyWarning}{Warning}
this performs an exact comparison, which is generally a bad idea with floating-\/point types. In order to check for equality between two vectors or matrices with floating-\/point coefficients, it is generally a far better idea to use a fuzzy comparison as provided by \doxylink{classEigen_1_1DenseBase_af3793521d788a946cb9c5f4f92bab4d3}{is\+Approx()} and \doxylink{classEigen_1_1DenseBase_acc982903f94ed372fafa901e6822ae8d}{is\+Much\+Smaller\+Than()}.
\end{DoxyWarning}

\end{DoxyVerbInclude}

template$<$int Index\+\_\+$>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a9efec3cfd22b9a33bead9c6718d128da}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Matrix\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::template \mbox{\hyperlink{structEigen_1_1MatrixBase_1_1DiagonalIndexReturnType}{Diagonal\+Index\+Return\+Type}}$<$ Index\+\_\+ $>$\+::\+Type \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Eigen\+::\+Matrix\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::diagonal (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
an expression of the {\itshape Diag\+Index-\/th} sub or super diagonal of the matrix {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this} 
\end{DoxyReturn}
{\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this} is not required to be square.

The template parameter {\itshape Diag\+Index} represent a super diagonal if {\itshape Diag\+Index} \texorpdfstring{$>$}{>} 0 and a sub diagonal otherwise. {\itshape Diag\+Index} == 0 is equivalent to the main diagonal.

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{diagonal()}{diagonal()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [11/14]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a74bbbfeceaf3f9204643f61c2ed271d5} 
template$<$typename Derived $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a9efec3cfd22b9a33bead9c6718d128da}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Matrix\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a0707310a4964d93cf2785528fd889a19}{\+::\+Diagonal\+Dynamic\+Index\+Return\+Type}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Eigen\+::\+Matrix\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::diagonal (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceEigen_a62e77e0933482dafde8fe197d9a2cfde}{Index}}}]{index}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
an expression of the {\itshape Diag\+Index-\/th} sub or super diagonal of the matrix {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this} 
\end{DoxyReturn}
{\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this} is not required to be square.

The template parameter {\itshape Diag\+Index} represent a super diagonal if {\itshape Diag\+Index} \texorpdfstring{$>$}{>} 0 and a sub diagonal otherwise. {\itshape Diag\+Index} == 0 is equivalent to the main diagonal.

\end{DoxyCodeInclude}
 Output\+:

\end{DoxyVerbInclude}

\Hypertarget{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a30430fa3d5b4e74d312fd4f502ac984d}\index{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$}!eigenvalues@{eigenvalues}}
\index{eigenvalues@{eigenvalues}!Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{eigenvalues()}{eigenvalues()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a30430fa3d5b4e74d312fd4f502ac984d} 
template$<$typename Derived $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Matrix\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a508ff602ab3732a61a8bf9a8bcddca28}{\+::\+Eigenvalues\+Return\+Type}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Eigen\+::\+Matrix\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::eigenvalues (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}



Computes the eigenvalues of a matrix. 

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Column vector containing the eigenvalues.
\end{DoxyReturn}
\textbackslash{}eigenvalues\+\_\+module This function computes the eigenvalues with the help of the \doxylink{classEigen_1_1EigenSolver}{Eigen\+Solver} class (for real matrices) or the \doxylink{classEigen_1_1ComplexEigenSolver}{Complex\+Eigen\+Solver} class (for complex matrices).

The eigenvalues are repeated according to their algebraic multiplicity, so there are as many eigenvalues as rows in the matrix.

The \doxylink{classEigen_1_1SelfAdjointView}{Self\+Adjoint\+View} class provides a better algorithm for selfadjoint matrices.

\end{DoxyCodeInclude}

\end{DoxyVerbInclude}

template$<$typename Derived $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a9efec3cfd22b9a33bead9c6718d128da}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC}} \mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_af2b60117c00a6e75812de43bfe7db3b1}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+STRONG\+\_\+\+INLINE}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1DenseBase_ab4c6aa4015d8a974d950fe04981372ed}{Eval\+Return\+Type}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1DenseBase}{Eigen\+::\+Dense\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::eval (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
the matrix or vector obtained by evaluating this expression.
\end{DoxyReturn}
Notice that in the case of a plain matrix or vector (not an expression) this function just returns a const reference, in order to avoid a useless copy.

\begin{DoxyWarning}{Warning}
Be careful with \doxylink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a5df64c66228ba75bbc66db2584185527}{eval()} and the auto C++ keyword, as detailed in this \doxylink{}{page }. 
\end{DoxyWarning}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
an expression of the identity matrix (not necessarily square).
\end{DoxyReturn}
This variant is only for fixed-\/size \doxylink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Matrix\+Base} types. For dynamic-\/size types, you need to use the variant taking size arguments.

\Hypertarget{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_ae717f291d83ab229ae64a4903d9f987d}\index{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$}!Identity@{Identity}}
\index{Identity@{Identity}!Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Identity()}{Identity()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [3/4]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_ae717f291d83ab229ae64a4903d9f987d} 
template$<$typename Derived $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a9efec3cfd22b9a33bead9c6718d128da}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC}} \mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_af2b60117c00a6e75812de43bfe7db3b1}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+STRONG\+\_\+\+INLINE}} const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Matrix\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_ae62b01d6b4c74e1341751eafdd4c571b}{\+::\+Identity\+Return\+Type}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Eigen\+::\+Matrix\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::\+Identity (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceEigen_a62e77e0933482dafde8fe197d9a2cfde}{Index}}}]{rows}{, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceEigen_a62e77e0933482dafde8fe197d9a2cfde}{Index}}}]{cols}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [static]}}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
an expression of the identity matrix (not necessarily square).
\end{DoxyReturn}
The parameters {\itshape rows} and {\itshape cols} are the number of rows and of columns of the returned matrix. Must be compatible with this \doxylink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Matrix\+Base} type.

This variant is meant to be used for dynamic-\/size matrix types. For fixed-\/size types, it is redundant to pass {\itshape rows} and {\itshape cols} as arguments, so \doxylink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a2ef43190f3aba0aef0cf1030d46d0ca7}{Identity()} should be used instead.

\end{DoxyCodeInclude}

\Hypertarget{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_add090d35d12d42d01eba1a24f22cf8f3}\index{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$}!inverse@{inverse}}
\index{inverse@{inverse}!Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{inverse()}{inverse()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_add090d35d12d42d01eba1a24f22cf8f3} 
template$<$typename Derived $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a9efec3cfd22b9a33bead9c6718d128da}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC}} const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1Inverse}{Inverse}}$<$ Derived $>$ \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Eigen\+::\+Matrix\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::inverse (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

\textbackslash{}lu\+\_\+module

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
the matrix inverse of this matrix.
\end{DoxyReturn}
For small fixed sizes up to 4x4, this method uses cofactors. In the general case, this method uses class \doxylink{classEigen_1_1PartialPivLU}{Partial\+Piv\+LU}.

\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
This matrix must be invertible, otherwise the result is undefined. If you need an invertibility check, do the following\+: \begin{DoxyItemize}
\item for fixed sizes up to 4x4, use \doxylink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a7baaf2fdec0191a2166cf9fd84a2dcb2}{compute\+Inverse\+And\+Det\+With\+Check()}. \item for the general case, use class \doxylink{classEigen_1_1FullPivLU}{Full\+Piv\+LU}.\end{DoxyItemize}
Example\+: 
\begin{DoxyCodeInclude}{0}

\end{DoxyCodeInclude}
 Output\+: 
\begin{DoxyVerbInclude}
\end{DoxyVerbInclude}

\end{DoxyNote}

\Hypertarget{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a8a7ee34ce202cac3eeea9cf20c9e4833}\index{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$}!isUnitary@{isUnitary}}
\index{isUnitary@{isUnitary}!Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{isUnitary()}{isUnitary()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a8a7ee34ce202cac3eeea9cf20c9e4833} 
template$<$typename Derived $>$ \\
bool \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Eigen\+::\+Matrix\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::is\+Unitary (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a04816f5030c114f446ab76a6cdf0f216}{Real\+Scalar}} \&}]{prec}{ = {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{structEigen_1_1NumTraits}{Num\+Traits}}$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_ac6c9fcfb905b0e2b83652e950a52246f}{Scalar}}$>$\+:\+:dummy\+\_\+precision()}}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
true if \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this is approximately an unitary matrix, within the precision given by {\itshape prec}. In the case where the {\itshape Scalar} type is real numbers, a unitary matrix is an orthogonal matrix, whence the name.
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
This can be used to check whether a family of vectors forms an orthonormal basis. Indeed, {\ttfamily m.\+is\+Unitary()} returns true if and only if the columns (equivalently, the rows) of m form an orthonormal basis.
\end{DoxyNote}

\Hypertarget{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_aa394a9eeea28fee3c4624a5f9c666c7d}\index{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$}!lazyAssign@{lazyAssign}}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{lazyAssign()}{lazyAssign()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_aa394a9eeea28fee3c4624a5f9c666c7d} 
template$<$typename Derived $>$ \\
template$<$typename Other\+Derived $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a215b4c2831ed3631e9149b53a8ecb878}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEPRECATED}} \mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a9efec3cfd22b9a33bead9c6718d128da}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC}} Derived \& \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1DenseBase}{Eigen\+::\+Dense\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::lazy\+Assign (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1DenseBase}{Dense\+Base}}$<$ Other\+Derived $>$ \&}]{other}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyRefDesc}{Deprecated}
\item[\mbox{\hyperlink{deprecated__deprecated000003}{Deprecated}}]\end{DoxyRefDesc}
\Hypertarget{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_af2c6c32531e9bde57feef6201a241040}\index{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$}!lazyProduct@{lazyProduct}}
\index{lazyProduct@{lazyProduct}!Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{lazyProduct()}{lazyProduct()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/3]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_af2c6c32531e9bde57feef6201a241040} 
template$<$typename Derived $>$ \\
template$<$typename Other\+Derived $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a9efec3cfd22b9a33bead9c6718d128da}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC}} \mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_af2b60117c00a6e75812de43bfe7db3b1}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+STRONG\+\_\+\+INLINE}} const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1Product}{Product}}$<$ Derived, Other\+Derived, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceEigen_a15a3e26ba06f3c60d2f2e46f56045f27a88338d2855e65a687d92f99255e7a8cc}{Lazy\+Product}} $>$ \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Eigen\+::\+Matrix\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::lazy\+Product (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Matrix\+Base}}$<$ Other\+Derived $>$ \&}]{other}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
an expression of the matrix product of {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this} and {\itshape other} without implicit evaluation.
\end{DoxyReturn}
The returned product will behave like any other expressions\+: the coefficients of the product will be computed once at a time as requested. This might be useful in some extremely rare cases when only a small and no coherent fraction of the result\textquotesingle{}s coefficients have to be computed.

\begin{DoxyWarning}{Warning}
This version of the matrix product can be much much slower. So use it only if you know what you are doing and that you measured a true speed improvement.
\end{DoxyWarning}

\Hypertarget{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_aa37effc4e7b8d456a092f980a74b95d2}\index{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$}!lpNorm@{lpNorm}}
\index{lpNorm@{lpNorm}!Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{lpNorm()}{lpNorm()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/3]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_aa37effc4e7b8d456a092f980a74b95d2} 
template$<$typename Derived $>$ \\
template$<$int p$>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a9efec3cfd22b9a33bead9c6718d128da}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC}} \mbox{\hyperlink{structEigen_1_1NumTraits}{Num\+Traits}}$<$ typenameinternal\+::traits$<$ Derived $>$\mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_ac6c9fcfb905b0e2b83652e950a52246f}{\+::\+Scalar}} $>$\+::\+Real \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Eigen\+::\+Matrix\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::lp\+Norm (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
the {\bfseries{coefficient-\/wise}} $ \ell^p $ norm of {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this}, that is, returns the p-\/th root of the sum of the p-\/th powers of the absolute values of the coefficients of {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this}. If {\itshape p} is the special value {\itshape \doxylink{namespaceEigen_a7951593b031e13d90223c83d022ce99e}{Eigen\+::\+Infinity}}, this function returns the $ \ell^\infty $ norm, that is the maximum of the absolute values of the coefficients of {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this}.
\end{DoxyReturn}
In all cases, if {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this} is empty, then the value 0 is returned.

\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
For matrices, this function does not compute the \href{https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operator_norm}{\texttt{ operator-\/norm}}. That is, if {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this} is a matrix, then its coefficients are interpreted as a 1D vector. Nonetheless, you can easily compute the 1-\/norm and $\infty$-\/norm matrix operator norms using \doxylink{}{partial reductions }.
\end{DoxyNote}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\doxylink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_ace03acc2885d22588472ae898a689093}{norm()} 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

Computes the elementary reflector H such that\+: $ H *this = [ beta 0 ... 0]^T $ where the transformation H is\+: $ H = I - tau v v^*$ and the vector v is\+: $ v^T = [1 essential^T] $

Computes the elementary reflector H such that\+: $ H *this = [ beta 0 ... 0]^T $ where the transformation H is\+: $ H = I - tau v v^*$ and the vector v is\+: $ v^T = [1 essential^T] $

\Hypertarget{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a7f15120bb9c88c30aa5d993bd6d138e1}\index{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$}!noalias@{noalias}}
\index{noalias@{noalias}!Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{noalias()}{noalias()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a7f15120bb9c88c30aa5d993bd6d138e1} 
template$<$typename Derived $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1NoAlias}{No\+Alias}}$<$ Derived, \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Matrix\+Base}} $>$ \mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a9efec3cfd22b9a33bead9c6718d128da}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Eigen\+::\+Matrix\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::noalias (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
a pseudo expression of {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this} with an operator= assuming no aliasing between {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this} and the source expression.
\end{DoxyReturn}
More precisely, \doxylink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a7f15120bb9c88c30aa5d993bd6d138e1}{noalias()} allows to bypass the Eval\+Before\+Assign\+Bit flag. Currently, even though several expressions may alias, only product expressions have this flag. Therefore, \doxylink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a7f15120bb9c88c30aa5d993bd6d138e1}{noalias()} is only useful when the source expression contains a matrix product.

Here are some examples where noalias is useful\+: 
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{D.noalias()\ \ =\ A\ *\ B;}
\DoxyCodeLine{D.noalias()\ +=\ A.transpose()\ *\ B;}
\DoxyCodeLine{D.noalias()\ -\/=\ 2\ *\ A\ *\ B.adjoint();}

\end{DoxyCode}


On the other hand the following example will lead to a {\bfseries{wrong}} result\+: 
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{A.noalias()\ =\ A\ *\ B;}

\end{DoxyCode}
 because the result matrix A is also an operand of the matrix product. Therefore, there is no alternative than evaluating A \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} B in a temporary, that is the default behavior when you write\+: 
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{A\ =\ A\ *\ B;}

\end{DoxyCode}


\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
class \doxylink{classEigen_1_1NoAlias}{No\+Alias} 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\Hypertarget{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_ace03acc2885d22588472ae898a689093}\index{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$}!norm@{norm}}
\index{norm@{norm}!Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{norm()}{norm()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_ace03acc2885d22588472ae898a689093} 
template$<$typename Derived $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a9efec3cfd22b9a33bead9c6718d128da}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC}} \mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_af2b60117c00a6e75812de43bfe7db3b1}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+STRONG\+\_\+\+INLINE}} \mbox{\hyperlink{structEigen_1_1NumTraits}{Num\+Traits}}$<$ typenameinternal\+::traits$<$ Derived $>$\mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_ac6c9fcfb905b0e2b83652e950a52246f}{\+::\+Scalar}} $>$\+::\+Real \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Eigen\+::\+Matrix\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::norm (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
, for vectors, the {\itshape l2} norm of {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this}, and for matrices the Frobenius norm. In both cases, it consists in the square root of the sum of the square of all the matrix entries. For vectors, this is also equals to the square root of the dot product of {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this} with itself.
\end{DoxyReturn}

Normalizes the vector, i.\+e. divides it by its own norm.

\textbackslash{}only\+\_\+for\+\_\+vectors

\end{DoxyReturn}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a932a37b58d2bad69849a3a8809aaffac} 
template$<$typename Derived $>$ \\
template$<$typename Other\+Derived $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a9efec3cfd22b9a33bead9c6718d128da}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC}} bool \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Eigen\+::\+Matrix\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2plugins_2ArrayCwiseUnaryOps_8h_aa198852a6b380257ea3e34c8f7e6e250}{\+::operator!}}= (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Matrix\+Base}}$<$ Other\+Derived $>$ \&}]{other}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
true if at least one pair of coefficients of {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this} and {\itshape other} are not exactly equal to each other. 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxyWarning}{Warning}
When using floating point scalar values you probably should rather use a fuzzy comparison such as \doxylink{classEigen_1_1DenseBase_af3793521d788a946cb9c5f4f92bab4d3}{is\+Approx()} 
\end{DoxyWarning}

\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a9efec3cfd22b9a33bead9c6718d128da}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC}} bool \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Eigen\+::\+Matrix\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2plugins_2ArrayCwiseUnaryOps_8h_aa198852a6b380257ea3e34c8f7e6e250}{\+::operator!}}= (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Matrix\+Base}}$<$ Other\+Derived $>$ \&}]{other}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
true if at least one pair of coefficients of {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this} and {\itshape other} are not exactly equal to each other. 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxyWarning}{Warning}
When using floating point scalar values you probably should rather use a fuzzy comparison such as \doxylink{classEigen_1_1DenseBase_af3793521d788a946cb9c5f4f92bab4d3}{is\+Approx()} 
\end{DoxyWarning}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\doxylink{classEigen_1_1DenseBase_af3793521d788a946cb9c5f4f92bab4d3}{is\+Approx()}, operator== 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\Hypertarget{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a0ff9bc0b9bea2d0822a2bf3192783102}\index{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$}!operatorNorm@{operatorNorm}}
\index{operatorNorm@{operatorNorm}!Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{operatorNorm()}{operatorNorm()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a0ff9bc0b9bea2d0822a2bf3192783102} 
template$<$typename Derived $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Matrix\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a04816f5030c114f446ab76a6cdf0f216}{\+::\+Real\+Scalar}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Eigen\+::\+Matrix\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::operator\+Norm (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}



Computes the L2 operator norm. 

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Operator norm of the matrix.
\end{DoxyReturn}
\textbackslash{}eigenvalues\+\_\+module This function computes the L2 operator norm of a matrix, which is also known as the spectral norm. The norm of a matrix $ A $ is defined to be \[ \|A\|_2 = \max_x \frac{\|Ax\|_2}{\|x\|_2} \] where the maximum is over all vectors and the norm on the right is the Euclidean vector norm. The norm equals the largest singular value, which is the square root of the largest eigenvalue of the positive semi-\/definite matrix $ A^*A $.

The current implementation uses the eigenvalues of $ A^*A $, as computed by \doxylink{classEigen_1_1SelfAdjointView_a66a18e7f6619ebbd3532c93da1209871}{Self\+Adjoint\+View\+::eigenvalues()}, to compute the operator norm of a matrix. The \doxylink{classEigen_1_1SelfAdjointView}{Self\+Adjoint\+View} class provides a better algorithm for selfadjoint matrices.

\end{DoxyCodeInclude}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{sparseView()}{sparseView()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a320dd291cbf4339c6118c41521b75350} 
template$<$typename Derived $>$ \\
const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1SparseView}{Sparse\+View}}$<$ Derived $>$ \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Eigen\+::\+Matrix\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::sparse\+View (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_ac6c9fcfb905b0e2b83652e950a52246f}{Scalar}} \&}]{reference}{ = {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_ac6c9fcfb905b0e2b83652e950a52246f}{Scalar}}(0)}, }\item[{const typename \mbox{\hyperlink{structEigen_1_1NumTraits}{Num\+Traits}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_ac6c9fcfb905b0e2b83652e950a52246f}{Scalar}} $>$\+::\+Real \&}]{epsilon}{ = {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{structEigen_1_1NumTraits}{Num\+Traits}}$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_ac6c9fcfb905b0e2b83652e950a52246f}{Scalar}}$>$\+:\+:dummy\+\_\+precision()}}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
a sparse expression of the dense expression {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this} with values smaller than {\itshape reference} \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} {\itshape epsilon} removed.
\end{DoxyReturn}
This method is typically used when prototyping to convert a quickly assembled dense \doxylink{classEigen_1_1Matrix}{Matrix} {\ttfamily D} to a \doxylink{classEigen_1_1SparseMatrix}{Sparse\+Matrix} {\ttfamily S\+:} 
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{MatrixXd\ D(\mbox{\hyperlink{abseil-cpp_2absl_2container_2btree__test_8cc_a76f11d9a0a47b94f72c2d0e77fb32240}{n}},m);}
\DoxyCodeLine{SparseMatrix<double>\ S;}
\DoxyCodeLine{S\ =\ D.sparseView();\ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \textcolor{comment}{//\ suppress\ numerical\ zeros\ (exact)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{S\ =\ D.sparseView(reference);}
\DoxyCodeLine{S\ =\ D.sparseView(reference,epsilon);}

\end{DoxyCode}
 where {\itshape reference} is a meaningful non zero reference value, and {\itshape epsilon} is a tolerance factor defaulting to \doxylink{structEigen_1_1GenericNumTraits_aec48507dff26f2fdbb985a871f7f4eff}{Num\+Traits$<$\+Scalar$>$\+::dummy\+\_\+precision()}.

\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\Hypertarget{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a0afd613885f8d3a66978b1255b5887c1}\index{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$}!squaredNorm@{squaredNorm}}
\index{squaredNorm@{squaredNorm}!Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{squaredNorm()}{squaredNorm()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a0afd613885f8d3a66978b1255b5887c1} 
template$<$typename Derived $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a9efec3cfd22b9a33bead9c6718d128da}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC}} \mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_af2b60117c00a6e75812de43bfe7db3b1}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+STRONG\+\_\+\+INLINE}} \mbox{\hyperlink{structEigen_1_1NumTraits}{Num\+Traits}}$<$ typenameinternal\+::traits$<$ Derived $>$\mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_ac6c9fcfb905b0e2b83652e950a52246f}{\+::\+Scalar}} $>$\+::\+Real \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Eigen\+::\+Matrix\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::squared\+Norm (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
, for vectors, the squared {\itshape l2} norm of {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this}, and for matrices the squared Frobenius norm. In both cases, it consists in the sum of the square of all the matrix entries. For vectors, this is also equals to the dot product of {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this} with itself.
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}

\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\index{squaredNorm@{squaredNorm}!Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$}}

template$<$typename Derived $>$ \\

\Hypertarget{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a624431d9543dacf9aef2bee325a0686f}\index{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$}!stableNorm@{stableNorm}}
\index{stableNorm@{stableNorm}!Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$@{Eigen::MatrixBase$<$ Derived $>$}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{stableNorm()}{stableNorm()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a624431d9543dacf9aef2bee325a0686f} 
template$<$typename Derived $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{structEigen_1_1NumTraits}{Num\+Traits}}$<$ typenameinternal\+::traits$<$ Derived $>$\mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_ac6c9fcfb905b0e2b83652e950a52246f}{\+::\+Scalar}} $>$\+::\+Real \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Eigen\+::\+Matrix\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::stable\+Norm (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
the {\itshape l2} norm of {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this} avoiding underflow and overflow. This version use a blockwise two passes algorithm\+: 1 -\/ find the absolute largest coefficient {\ttfamily s} 2 -\/ compute $ s \Vert \frac{*this}{s} \Vert $ in a standard way
\end{DoxyReturn}
For architecture/scalar types supporting vectorization, this version is faster than \doxylink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a4a3ac99e4cd767a110c84421dda22ab1}{blue\+Norm()}. Otherwise the \doxylink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a4a3ac99e4cd767a110c84421dda22ab1}{blue\+Norm()} is much faster.

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\doxylink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_ace03acc2885d22588472ae898a689093}{norm()}, \doxylink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a4a3ac99e4cd767a110c84421dda22ab1}{blue\+Norm()}, \doxylink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a54e11547512ffc3b211cc0ee6caba98c}{hypot\+Norm()} 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

template$<$typename Derived $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a9efec3cfd22b9a33bead9c6718d128da}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC}} \mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_af2b60117c00a6e75812de43bfe7db3b1}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+STRONG\+\_\+\+INLINE}} void \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Eigen\+::\+Matrix\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::stable\+Normalize (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Normalizes the vector while avoid underflow and overflow

\textbackslash{}only\+\_\+for\+\_\+vectors

This method is analogue to the \doxylink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_a82aab8b1e4a00beea9d8be19eb2f9f6d}{normalize()} method, but it reduces the risk of underflow and overflow when computing the norm.

\begin{DoxyWarning}{Warning}
If the input vector is too small (i.\+e., this-\/\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}\doxylink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_ace03acc2885d22588472ae898a689093}{norm()}==0), then {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this} is left unchanged.
\end{DoxyWarning}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}

\end{DoxySeeAlso}

template$<$typename Derived $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a9efec3cfd22b9a33bead9c6718d128da}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC}} \mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_af2b60117c00a6e75812de43bfe7db3b1}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+STRONG\+\_\+\+INLINE}} const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Matrix\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_aaf60e25933045913a5ee91ef197878df}{\+::\+Plain\+Object}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Eigen\+::\+Matrix\+Base}}$<$ Derived $>$\+::stable\+Normalized (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
an expression of the quotient of {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this} by its own norm while avoiding underflow and overflow.
\end{DoxyReturn}
\textbackslash{}only\+\_\+for\+\_\+vectors

This method is analogue to the \doxylink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_ab0b6f60e35452acd779e340856fde121}{normalized()} method, but it reduces the risk of underflow and overflow when computing the norm.

\begin{DoxyWarning}{Warning}
If the input vector is too small (i.\+e., this-\/\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}\doxylink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_ace03acc2885d22588472ae898a689093}{norm()}==0), then this function returns a copy of the input.
\end{DoxyWarning}

an expression of a triangular view extracted from the current matrix
\end{DoxyReturn}
The parameter {\itshape Mode} can have the following values\+: {\ttfamily \doxylink{group__enums_gga39e3366ff5554d731e7dc8bb642f83cda6bcb58be3b8b8ec84859ce0c5ac0aaec}{Upper}}, {\ttfamily \doxylink{group__enums_gga39e3366ff5554d731e7dc8bb642f83cdae38aad7d66fecfb213fce453edff4c7a}{Strictly\+Upper}}, {\ttfamily \doxylink{group__enums_gga39e3366ff5554d731e7dc8bb642f83cda8b0b63ff46dcd7377b59df14e0562fc1}{Unit\+Upper}}, {\ttfamily \doxylink{group__enums_gga39e3366ff5554d731e7dc8bb642f83cda891792b8ed394f7607ab16dd716f60e6}{Lower}}, {\ttfamily \doxylink{group__enums_gga39e3366ff5554d731e7dc8bb642f83cda00aa79c8865ada1584c4d57bcd93299f}{Strictly\+Lower}}, {\ttfamily \doxylink{group__enums_gga39e3366ff5554d731e7dc8bb642f83cda8155cfdfde9e75e7144dff0393d17181}{Unit\+Lower}}.
